<img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />&#160;0.894<br /><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:darkgreen">very high</span></span>&#160;·&#160;<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">59th</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td>

<a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:VI" title="ISO 3166-2:VI">VI</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td>
<div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/.vi" title=".vi">.vi</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="line-height:11pt"><b>Website</b><br /><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.vi.gov/">www.vi.gov</a></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>United States Virgin Islands</b> (<b>USVI</b>; also called the <b>American Virgin Islands</b>), officially the <b>Virgin Islands of the United States</b>, is a group of islands in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">unincorporated and organized territory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The islands are geographically part of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands archipelago</a> and are located in the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>.
</p><p>The U.S. Virgin Islands consists of the main islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint John</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Thomas</a>, and many other surrounding <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_islands_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="List of minor islands of the United States Virgin Islands">minor islands</a>. The total land area of the territory is 133.73 square miles (346.36&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The territory's capital is <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Amalie,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Charlotte Amalie, U.S. Virgin Islands">Charlotte Amalie</a> on the island of St. Thomas. 
</p><p>Previously known as the <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indies" title="Danish West Indies">Danish West Indies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Kingdom of Denmark–Norway</a>, they were sold to the United States by <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Danish_West_Indies" title="Treaty of the Danish West Indies">Treaty of the Danish West Indies</a> of 1916. They are classified by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> as a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">Non-Self-Governing Territory</a>, and are currently an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_territories_of_the_United_States" title="Unincorporated territories of the United States">organized, unincorporated United States territory</a>. The U.S. Virgin Islands are organized under the 1954 <a href="/wiki/Revised_Organic_Act_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Revised Organic Act of the Virgin Islands">Revised Organic Act of the Virgin Islands</a> and have since held five constitutional conventions.  The last and only proposed Constitution, adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Constitutional_Convention_of_the_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands">Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands</a> in 2009, was rejected by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">US Congress</a> in 2010, which urged the convention to reconvene to address the concerns Congress and the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Barack_Obama" title="Presidency of Barack Obama">Obama Administration</a> had with the proposed document. The Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands met in October 2012 to address these concerns, but was not able to produce a revised Constitution before its October 31 deadline.
</p><p>In 2010 the population was 106,405,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and mostly <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a>. Tourism and related categories are the primary economic activity, employing a high percentage of the <i>civilian</i> non-farm labor force that totaled 42,752 persons in 2016. (The total non-farm labor force was 48,278 persons.) Private sector jobs made up 71 percent of the total workforce. The average private sector salary was $34,088 and the average public sector salary was $52,572.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a May 2016 report, some 11,000 people were categorized as being involved in some aspect of agriculture in the first half of 2016 but this category makes up a small part of the total economy. (The islands have a significant rum manufacturing sector.) At that time, there were approximately 607 manufacturing jobs and 1,487 natural resource and construction jobs. The single largest employer was the government.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In mid-February 2017, the USVI was facing a financial crisis due to a very high debt level of $2 billion and a structural budget deficit of $110 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Baribeau_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baribeau-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gilbert_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilbert-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Then early August 2017, the U.S. Virgin Islands government was rejected from the bond market.
</p><p>In September 2017, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> slammed the U.S. Virgin Islands as Category 5 storms causing extensive damage to buildings and the island’s power grid. More than 3,200 Virgin Islanders moved to the US mainland to seek job opportunities and a better life.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(January 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="History of the United States Virgin Islands">History of the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>The U.S. Virgin Islands were originally inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">Ciboney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Carib</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawaks</a>. The islands were named by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> on his second voyage in 1493 for <a href="/wiki/Saint_Ursula" title="Saint Ursula">Saint Ursula</a> and her <a href="/wiki/Virginity" title="Virginity">virgin</a> followers. Over the next two hundred years, the islands were held by many European powers, including Spain, Great Britain, the Netherlands, France, and <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Denmark–Norway</a>. In 1927, the inhabitants of the U.S. Virgin Islands were granted American citizenship.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_India_Company" title="Danish West India Company">Danish West India Company</a> settled on St. Thomas in 1672, settled on St. John in 1694, and purchased St. Croix from France in 1733.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The islands became royal Danish colonies in 1754, named the Danish West Indian Islands (<a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <i lang="da">De dansk-vestindiske øer</i>). <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">Sugarcane</a>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slave</a> labor, drove the islands' <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economy</a> during the 18th and early 19th centuries, until the <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline#1800–1849" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolition of slavery timeline">abolition of slavery</a> by Governor <a href="/wiki/Peter_von_Scholten" title="Peter von Scholten">Peter von Scholten</a> on July 3, 1848.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_India_Company" title="Danish West India Company">Danish West India and Guinea Company</a> are also credited with naming the island St. John (Danish: Sankt Jan). The Danish crown took full control of St. John in 1754 along with St. Thomas and St. Croix. Sugarcane <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">plantations</a> such as the famous Annaberg Sugar Plantation were established in great numbers on St. John because of the intense heat and fertile terrain that provided ideal growing conditions. The establishment of sugarcane plantations also led to the buying of more slaves from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. In 1733, St. John was the site of one of the <a href="/wiki/1733_slave_insurrection_on_St._John" title="1733 slave insurrection on St. John">first significant slave rebellions</a> in the New World when Akwamu slaves from the Gold Coast took over the island for six months.
</p><p>The Danish were able to defeat the enslaved Africans with help from the French in <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>. Instead of allowing themselves to be recaptured, more than a dozen of the ringleaders shot themselves before the French forces could capture them and call them to account for their activities during the period of rebel control. It is estimated that by 1775, slaves outnumbered the Danish settlers by a ratio of 5:1. The indigenous Caribs and Arawaks were also used as slave labor to the point of the entire native population being absorbed into the larger groups. Slavery was abolished in the Virgin Islands on July 3, 1848.
</p><p>Although some plantation owners refused to accept the abolition, some 5,000 Black people were freed while another 17,000 remained enslaved. In that era, slaves labored mainly on sugar plantations. Other crops included cotton and indigo. Over the following years, strict labor laws were implemented several times, leading planters to abandon their estates, causing a significant drop in population and the overall economy.  In the late 1800s, numerous natural disasters added to diminish the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2017)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> For the remainder of the period of Danish rule the islands were not economically viable and significant transfers were made from the Danish state budgets to the authorities in the islands. In 1867 a treaty to sell St. Thomas and St. John to the United States was agreed, but the sale was never effected.<sup id="cite_ref-Danish_National_Archives_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Danish_National_Archives-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A number of reforms aimed at reviving the islands' economy were attempted, but none had great success. A second draft treaty to sell the islands to the United States was negotiated in 1902 but was defeated in the upper house of the Danish parliament in a tie vote (because the opposition carried a 97-year-old life member into the chamber).<sup id="cite_ref-Danish_National_Archives_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Danish_National_Archives-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2940" data-file-height="1952" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marilyn" title="Hurricane Marilyn">Hurricane Marilyn</a> on the island of St. Thomas, 1995</div></div></div>
<p>The onset of World War I brought the reforms to a close and again left the islands isolated and exposed. During the <a href="/wiki/Submarine_warfare" title="Submarine warfare">submarine warfare</a> phases of the war, the United States, fearing that the islands might be seized by Germany as a submarine base, again approached Denmark about buying them. After a few months of negotiations, a selling price of $25&#160;million in United States gold coin was agreed, equivalent to $562.23&#160;million in 2017 dollars. At the same time the economics of continued possession weighed heavily on the minds of Danish decision makers, and a consensus in favor of selling emerged in the Danish parliament.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Danish_West_Indies" title="Treaty of the Danish West Indies">Treaty of the Danish West Indies</a> was signed in August 1916,<sup id="cite_ref-treaty_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treaty-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> with a <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indian_Islands_sale_referendum,_1916" title="Danish West Indian Islands sale referendum, 1916">Danish referendum</a> held in December 1916 to confirm the decision. The deal was finalized on January 17, 1917, when the United States and Denmark exchanged their respective treaty ratifications. The United States took possession of the islands on March 31, 1917 and the territory was renamed the Virgin Islands of the United States. Every year <a href="/wiki/Transfer_Day" title="Transfer Day">Transfer Day</a> is recognized as a holiday, to commemorate the acquisition of the islands by the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Transfer_Day_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Transfer_Day-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> US citizenship was granted to the inhabitants of the islands in 1927. The US dollar was adopted in the territory in 1934<sup id="cite_ref-Report_of_the_Governor_of_the_Virgin_Islands_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Report_of_the_Governor_of_the_Virgin_Islands-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and from 1935 to 1939 the islands were a part of the <a href="/wiki/Customs_territory" title="Customs territory">United States customs area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Statistical_Abstract_of_the_United_States_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistical_Abstract_of_the_United_States-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Water_Island,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Water Island, U.S. Virgin Islands">Water Island</a>, a small island to the south of St. Thomas, was initially administered by the US federal government and did not become a part of the United States Virgin Islands territory until 1996, when 50 acres (20&#160;ha) of land was transferred to the territorial government. The remaining 200 acres (81&#160;ha) of the island were purchased from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">United States Department of the Interior</a> in May 2005 for $10, a transaction that marked the official change in jurisdiction.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> struck the U.S. Virgin Islands in 1989, causing catastrophic physical and economic damage, particularly on the island of St. Croix.  The territory was again struck by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marilyn" title="Hurricane Marilyn">Hurricane Marilyn</a> in 1995, killing eight people and causing more than $2 billion in damage. The islands were again struck by Hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bertha_(1996)" title="Hurricane Bertha (1996)">Bertha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Georges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Lenny</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Omar" title="Hurricane Omar">Omar</a> in 1996, 1998, 1999, and 2008, respectively, but damage was not as severe in those storms.  In 2017, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> caused catastrophic damage to St. John and St. Thomas; just days later, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>'s eyewall crossed over St. Croix.
</p><p>Until February 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Hovensa" title="Hovensa">Hovensa</a> plant located on St. Croix was one of the world's largest petroleum refineries and contributed about 20% of the territory's GDP. The facility stopped exporting petroleum products in 2014. In the final year of full refinery operations, the value of exported petroleum products was $12.7 billion (2011 fiscal year).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After being shut down, it has operated as no more than an oil storage facility; the closure had provoked a local economic crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2017, two weeks after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> hit St. Thomas and St. John while a Category 5 hurricane, Hurricane Maria's weaker outer eyewall was reported by the National Hurricane Center to have crossed St. Croix while the hurricane was at Category 5 intensity.  Sustained winds at the <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Point_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Sandy Point National Wildlife Refuge">Sandy Point National Wildlife Refuge</a> on St. Croix reached 99 to 104&#160;mph (159 to 167&#160;km/h) and gusted to 137&#160;mph (220&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Weather stations on St. Croix recorded 5 and 10 inches of rain from the hurricane, and estimates for St. John and St. Thomas were somewhat less.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The hurricane killed two people, both in their homes: one person drowned and another was trapped by a mudslide.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  A third person had a fatal heart attack during the hurricane.<sup id="cite_ref-StCroixHeartAttack_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StCroixHeartAttack-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The hurricane caused extensive and severe damage to St. Croix.  After both hurricanes, the office of V.I. congresswoman <a href="/wiki/Stacey_Plaskett" title="Stacey Plaskett">Stacey Plaskett</a> stated that 90% of buildings in the Virgin Islands were damaged or destroyed and 13,000 of those buildings had lost their roofs.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The Luis Hospital suffered roof damage and flooding, but remained operational.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Geography of the United States Virgin Islands">Geography of the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png/260px-Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png" width="260" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c5/Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="353" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the United States Virgin Islands</div></div></div>
<p>The U.S. Virgin Islands are in the Atlantic Ocean, about 40 miles (60&#160;km) east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and immediately west of the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>. They share the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Islands Archipelago">Virgin Islands Archipelago</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican Virgin Islands">Puerto Rican Virgin Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a> (administered by Puerto Rico), and the British Virgin Islands.
</p><p>The territory consists of three main islands: St. Thomas, St. John, and St. Croix, as well as several <a href="/wiki/Islands_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Islands of the United States Virgin Islands">dozen smaller islands</a>. The main islands have nicknames often used by locals: "Twin City" (St. Croix), "Rock City" (St. Thomas) and "Love City" (St. John).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The combined land area of the islands is roughly twice the size of Washington, D.C.
</p><p>The U.S. Virgin Islands are known for <a href="/wiki/List_of_beaches_in_the_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="List of beaches in the U.S. Virgin Islands">their white sand beaches</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Magens_Bay" title="Magens Bay">Magens Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trunk_Bay" title="Trunk Bay">Trunk Bay</a>, and deepwater harbors along the <a href="/wiki/Anegada_Passage" title="Anegada Passage">Anegada Passage</a>, including Charlotte Amalie and <a href="/wiki/Christiansted,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Christiansted, U.S. Virgin Islands">Christiansted</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Like most Caribbean islands, the islands of the Virgin Islands, including St. Thomas, are volcanic in origin and hilly. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Crown_Mountain_(United_States_Virgin_Islands)" title="Crown Mountain (United States Virgin Islands)">Crown Mountain</a>, St. Thomas (1,555&#160;ft or 474&#160;m).
</p><p>St. Croix, the largest of the U.S. Virgin Islands, lies to the south and has a flatter terrain due to being coral in origin. The <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> manages more than half of St. John, nearly all of <a href="/wiki/Hassel_Island,_United_States_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Hassel Island, United States Virgin Islands">Hassel Island</a>, and many acres of <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a>. (<i>See also</i> <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_National_Park" title="Virgin Islands National Park">Virgin Islands National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Coral_Reef_National_Monument" title="Virgin Islands Coral Reef National Monument">Virgin Islands Coral Reef National Monument</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buck_Island_Reef_National_Monument" title="Buck Island Reef National Monument">Buck Island Reef National Monument</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christiansted_National_Historic_Site" title="Christiansted National Historic Site">Christiansted National Historic Site</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salt_River_Bay_National_Historical_Park_and_Ecological_Preserve" title="Salt River Bay National Historical Park and Ecological Preserve">Salt River Bay National Historical Park and Ecological Preserve</a>.)
</p><p>The U.S. Virgin Islands lie on the boundary of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="North American plate">North American plate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>. Natural hazards include <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquakes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">hurricanes</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The United States Virgin Islands enjoy a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>, with little seasonal change throughout the year. Rainfall is concentrated in the high sun period (May through October), while in the winter the northeast <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> prevail. Summer and winter high temperatures differ by 5&#160;°F (3&#160;°C) or less on average.
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of the United States Virgin Islands">Climate of the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Politics of the United States Virgin Islands">Politics of the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Political party strength in the United States Virgin Islands">Political party strength in the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg/220px-Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg" width="220" height="73" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg/330px-Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg/440px-Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1212" data-file-height="402" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlotte_Amalie_Wade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Amalie,_United_States_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlotte Amalie, United States Virgin Islands">Charlotte Amalie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">St. Thomas</a>, the Islands' capital</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christiansted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Christiansted.jpg/220px-Christiansted.jpg" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Christiansted.jpg/330px-Christiansted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/06/Christiansted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="180" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christiansted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Christiansted,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Christiansted, U.S. Virgin Islands">Christiansted</a>, the largest town on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a></div></div></div>
<p>The U.S. Virgin Islands are an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_territories_of_the_United_States" title="Unincorporated territories of the United States">organized, unincorporated United States territory</a>. Although they are <a href="/wiki/United_States_nationality_law" title="United States nationality law">US citizens</a>, US Virgin Islanders residing in the territory are ineligible to vote for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">President of the United States</a>. They are, however, eligible to vote if they become residents of mainland US states.
</p><p>The US Democratic and Republican parties allow U.S. Virgin Islands citizens to vote in their presidential primary elections for delegates to the respective national conventions.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>People born in the U.S. Virgin Islands derive their US citizenship from Congressional statute.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main political parties in the U.S. Virgin Islands are the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Democratic Party of the Virgin Islands">Democratic Party of the Virgin Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Citizens_Movement" title="Independent Citizens Movement">Independent Citizens Movement</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Republican Party of the Virgin Islands">Republican Party of the Virgin Islands</a>. Additional candidates run as independents.
</p><p>At the national level, the U.S. Virgin Islands elect a <a href="/wiki/Delegate_(United_States_Congress)" class="mw-redirect" title="Delegate (United States Congress)">delegate to Congress</a> from their <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands%27s_at-large_congressional_district" title="United States Virgin Islands&#39;s at-large congressional district">congressional district</a>. The elected delegate, while able to vote in committee, cannot participate in floor votes. The current House of Representatives delegate is <a href="/wiki/Stacey_Plaskett" title="Stacey Plaskett">Stacey Plaskett</a>. Like other territories, the U.S. Virgin Islands does not have <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senate" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Senate">U.S. Senators</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the territorial level, fifteen <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Virgin_Islands_Senators" title="List of United States Virgin Islands Senators">senators</a> – seven from the district of St. Croix, seven from the district of St. Thomas and St. John, and one senator at-large who must be a resident of St. John – are elected for two-year terms to the <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Legislature of the Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands Legislature</a>. There is no limit as to the number of terms they can serve.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. Virgin Islands have elected a <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Virgin_Islands_Governors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United States Virgin Islands Governors">territorial governor</a> every four years since 1970. Previous governors were appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>.
</p><p>The U.S. Virgin Islands have a <a href="/wiki/District_Court_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="District Court of the Virgin Islands">District Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands_Superior_Court" title="United States Virgin Islands Superior Court">Superior Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Virgin Islands Supreme Court">Supreme Court</a>. The District Court is responsible for federal law, while the Superior Court is responsible for U.S. Virgin Islands law at the trial level and the Supreme Court is responsible for appeals from the Superior Court for all appeals filed on or after January 29, 2007.  Appeals filed prior to that date are heard by the Appellate Division of the District Court.  Appeals from the federal District Court are heard by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Third_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>.  District Court judges are appointed by the US president, while Superior Court and Supreme Court judges are appointed by the governor.
</p><p>On October 21, 1976, President <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> signed <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://legislink.org/us/pl-94-584">Pub.L. 94–584</a> authorizing the people of the United States Virgin Islands to organize a government pursuant to a constitution, which would be automatically approved if Congress did not act within 60 days. On May 26, 2009 the U.S. Virgin Islands Fifth Constitutional Convention adopted a proposed Constitution of the Virgin Islands, which was submitted by President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> to Congress on March 1, 2010. On June 30, 2010, President Obama signed <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://legislink.org/us/pl-111-194">Pub.L. 111–194</a> in which Congress rejected the proposed constitution and urged the constitutional convention to reconvene.
</p><p>As of early 2017, the territory still did not have its own constitution. Little has been achieved on this front since 2009 when a proposed constitution was contested by the US Justice Department on the grounds that the powers sought exceeded what would be considered allowable under territorial status.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In September 2012, the Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands was unable to come to a decision on the contents of a proposed constitution by the October 31 deadline.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_and_sub-districts_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Districts and sub-districts of the United States Virgin Islands">Districts and sub-districts of the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>Administratively, the U.S. Virgin Islands are <a href="/wiki/Districts_and_sub-districts_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Districts and sub-districts of the United States Virgin Islands">divided into two (2) districts</a>: the Saint Thomas &amp; Saint John district, and the Saint Croix district.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> However, the U.S. Census Bureau divides each of the 3 main islands into 3 separate statistical entities (which are further divided into twenty (20) sub-districts).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Below is the U.S. Census Bureau's division model.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Virgin_Islands_admin_divisions.png" class="image"><img alt="US Virgin Islands admin divisions.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/US_Virgin_Islands_admin_divisions.png/610px-US_Virgin_Islands_admin_divisions.png" width="610" height="371" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/US_Virgin_Islands_admin_divisions.png/915px-US_Virgin_Islands_admin_divisions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9f/US_Virgin_Islands_admin_divisions.png 2x" data-file-width="1022" data-file-height="621" /></a></div></div>

<p>Each of the 3 main islands of the U.S. Virgin Islands is counted as a <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county-equivalent</a> by the U.S. Census Bureau, with the following FIPS codes: 78010 for Saint Croix, 78020 for Saint John, and 78030 for Saint Thomas.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-statoid_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statoid-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While a Danish possession, the Islands were divided into "quarters" (five on St. John and nine on St. Croix) which were further divided into many dozens of "estates".  Estate names are still used to write addresses; estates and quarters are used in describing real estate, especially on St. John<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and St. Croix.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>  More densely populated towns such as <a href="/wiki/Frederiksted" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederiksted">Frederiksted</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christiansted" class="mw-redirect" title="Christiansted">Christiansted</a> on St. Croix were historically referred to as "districts", in contrast to the surrounding plantation land.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-determination">Self-determination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Self-determination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 1993 referendum on status attracted only 31.4% turnout, and so its results (in favor of the status quo) were considered void.  No further referenda have been scheduled since.
</p><p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Legislature of the Virgin Islands">25th Legislature of the Virgin Islands</a> established the Fifth Constitutional Convention, a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_convention_(political_meeting)" title="Constitutional convention (political meeting)">constitutional convention</a> gathered in order to draft a new constitution. In June 2009, Governor <a href="/wiki/John_de_Jongh" class="mw-redirect" title="John de Jongh">John de Jongh, Jr.</a> rejected the resulting constitutional draft, saying the terms of the document would "violate federal law, fail to defer to federal sovereignty and disregard basic civil rights."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> A lawsuit filed by members of the Convention to force Governor de Jongh to forward the document to President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> was ultimately successful. The President of the United States forwarded the proposal to Congress—which then had 60 days to approve or reject the document—in May 2010, along with a report noting concerns raised by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> and restating the issues noted by Governor de Jongh. A US Congressional resolution disapproving of the proposed constitution and requesting that the Fifth Constitutional Convention reconvene to consider changes to address these issues was signed into law by President Obama on June 30, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Months later, a federal lawsuit was filed in the <a href="/wiki/District_Court_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="District Court of the Virgin Islands">Federal District Court of the Virgin Islands</a> in 2011. The lawsuit claimed that the United States had to provide US Virgin Islanders with the ability to be represented in Congress and vote for US President. The case is Civil No. 3:11-cv-110, <i>Charles v. U.S. Federal Elections Commission et al.</i> (3:11-cv-00110-AET-RM). It alleged that racial discrimination present in an all-white and segregated US Congress of 1917 was the impetus to deny the right to vote to a majority non-white constituency. The case was ultimately dismissed and closed on August 16, 2012 by District Judge Anne E. Thompson from the <a href="/wiki/District_Court_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="District Court of the Virgin Islands">Federal District Court of the Virgin Islands</a>, Division of St. Croix.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands met in October 2012 but was not able to produce a revised Constitution before its October 31 deadline.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Special_Committee_on_Decolonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Committee on Decolonisation">Special Committee on Decolonisation</a>  recommended to the UN's General Assembly that this larger body should assist in "decolonization" and help the people of the territory to "determine freely their future political status". Specifically, the Special Committee recommended that the "views of the people of the United States Virgin Islands in respect of their right to self-determination should be ascertained" and that the UN should "actively pursue a public awareness campaign aimed at assisting the people of the United States Virgin Islands with their inalienable right to self-determination and in gaining a better understanding of the options for self-determination".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governors_of_the_U.S._Virgin_Islands">Governors of the U.S. Virgin Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Governors of the U.S. Virgin Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</p>
