<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands_Police_Department" title="United States Virgin Islands Police Department">United States Virgin Islands Police Department</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad,_St._Croix_(February_2012).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad%2C_St._Croix_%28February_2012%29.jpg/220px-U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad%2C_St._Croix_%28February_2012%29.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad%2C_St._Croix_%28February_2012%29.jpg/330px-U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad%2C_St._Croix_%28February_2012%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad%2C_St._Croix_%28February_2012%29.jpg/440px-U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad%2C_St._Croix_%28February_2012%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Virgin_Islands_Police_Department_officers_in_Christianstad,_St._Croix_(February_2012).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>USVI police officers in 2012</div></div></div>
<p>Law enforcement services are provided by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands_Police_Department" title="United States Virgin Islands Police Department">United States Virgin Islands Police Department</a> (USVIPD).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are some military facilities and personnel on the islands, supported by the United States government:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Reserve" title="United States Army Reserve">United States Army Reserve</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Army_National_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Islands Army National Guard">Virgin Islands Army National Guard</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Air_National_Guard" title="Virgin Islands Air National Guard">Virgin Islands Air National Guard</a>&#160;—— stationed at St Croix ANGS</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Army_National_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Islands Army National Guard">Virgin Islands Army National Guard</a>&#160;— stationed at St Croix ANGS</li>
<li>Lionel A. Jackson Readiness Center&#160;— shared facility for Army and Air units</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Although a public airport, <a href="/wiki/Henry_E._Rohlsen_Airport" title="Henry E. Rohlsen Airport">Henry E. Rohlsen Airport</a> has serviced aircraft from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Economy of the United States Virgin Islands">Economy of the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MagensBay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/MagensBay.jpg/220px-MagensBay.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/MagensBay.jpg/330px-MagensBay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/MagensBay.jpg/440px-MagensBay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MagensBay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Magens_Bay" title="Magens Bay">Magens Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">St. Thomas</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>A 2012 Economic report from the US Census Bureau indicated a total of 2,414 business establishments generating $6.8 billion in sales, employing 32,465 people and paying $1.1 billion in payroll per year. Between 2007 and 2012, sales declined by $12.6 billion, or 64.9 percent. (In 2007, total sales were $19.5 billion and the number employed was 35,300.)<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a report on the first half of 2016 by the VI Bureau of Economic Research, the unemployment rate was 11.5 percent. In May 2016 the islands' Bureau of Economic Research indicated that there were 37,613 non-agricultural wage and salary jobs in the islands. This report states that the "leisure and hospitality sector" employed an average of 7,333 people. The retail trade sector, which also serves many tourists, averaged another 5,913 jobs. Other categories which also include some tourism jobs include Arts and Entertainment (792 jobs), Accommodation and Food (6,541 jobs), Accommodation (3755 jobs), Food Services and Drink (2,766 jobs). A large percentage of the 37,613 non-farm workers are employed in dealing with tourists. Serving the local population is also part of the role of these sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_income">Personal income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Personal income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The median income for a household in the territory was $24,704, and the median income for a family was $28,553 according to the 2010 Census. Males had a median income of $28,309 versus $22,601 for females. The per capita income for the territory was $13,139. About 28.7% of families and 32.5% of the population were below the poverty line, including 41.7% of those less than 18 years old and 29.8% of those 65 or more years old. Nearly 70% of adults had at least a high school diploma and 19.2% had a bachelor's degree or higher.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_challenges">Financial challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Financial challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Analysts reviewing the economy often point to the closure of the HOVENSA oil refinery, the islands’ largest private sector employer, in early 2012 as having a major negative impact on the territory's economy. In late 2013, the Reserve Bank of New York’s Research and Statistics Group pointed out that manufacturing employment dropped by 50 percent in May 2012, and by another 4 percent by November 2012, and that the GDP fell by 13 percent, "mainly due to an 80 percent drop-off in exports (mostly refined petroleum)". On the other hand, tourism and some other service industries were growing. As well, the 2010 census indicated that a relatively high share of the adult population  is in the labor force: 66 percent, versus 65 percent on the mainland and well below 50 percent in Puerto Rico. The bottom line in this report however is that "it may also be worthwhile to look at the physical infrastructure and human capital built up over the years, with an eye toward using it for other types of productive economic activity".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A May 2016 report by Bloomberg expressed concern about the islands' tax-supported debt load.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> By January 23, 2017 this had increased to $2 billion. That translated to a per capita debt of $19,000, which was higher than the per capita debt in Puerto Rico which was undergoing a severe financial crisis at the time. A Debtwire analyst writing in <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> indicated that nothing short of a miracle would prevent a financial collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-Baribeau_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baribeau-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Another area of concern was the structural budget deficit which was at $110 million in mid February 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The government instituted a new law in March 2017 with new or increased taxes on rum, beer, tobacco products and sugary drinks, as well as internet purchases and timeshare unit owners.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tourism, trade, and other service-oriented industries are the primary economic activities, accounting for nearly 60% of the GDP.  Approximately 2.5 million tourists per year visit, most arriving on <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ships" class="mw-redirect" title="Cruise ships">cruise ships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  Such visitors do not spend large amounts of money ($146.70 each on average) but as a group, they contributed $339.8 million to the economy in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Garely_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garely-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, the travel industry warned in late 2014 that work needs to be done for USVI tourism practices to meet 21st century demands. "The needs of the community and the tourists may be diametrically opposed; however, for tourism to flourish cooperation is a necessity. From reduced energy costs to increased educational opportunities, from improved healthcare to a continued reduction in crime, these and many other challenges must be tackled. There is only now."<sup id="cite_ref-Garely_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garely-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Additionally, the islands frequently are a starting point for private <a href="/wiki/Yacht_charter" title="Yacht charter">yacht charters</a> to the neighboring <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>. Euromonitor indicates that over 50 percent of the workforce is employed in some tourism-related work.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Manufacturing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The manufacturing sector consists of mainly <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a> <a href="/wiki/Distillation" title="Distillation">distilling</a>. The agricultural sector is small, with most food being imported. International business and <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> are a small but growing component of the economy. Most energy is also generated from imported oil, leading to electricity costs four to five times higher than the U.S. mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The  Virgin Islands were the highest oil consumers per capita in the world in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Virgin Islands Water and Power Authority<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> also uses imported energy to operate its desalination facilities to provide fresh water.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>CIA World Factbook</i> lists the value of federal programs and grants&#160;— $241.4 million in 2013, 19.7% of the territory’s total revenues&#160;— and that "the economy remains relatively diversified. Along with the tourist industry, it appears that rum exports, trade, and services will be major income sources in future years".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_and_Trade">Tax and Trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tax and Trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The U.S. Virgin Islands are an independent <a href="/wiki/Customs_territory" title="Customs territory">customs territory</a> from the mainland United States and operate largely as a <a href="/wiki/Free_port" class="mw-redirect" title="Free port">free port</a>. US citizens thus do not have to clear customs when arriving in the U.S. Virgin Islands, but do when traveling to the mainland. Local residents are not subject to US federal income taxes on U.S. Virgin Islands source income; they pay taxes to the territory equal to what their federal taxes would be if they lived in a state.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_and_communications">Transportation and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transportation and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Transportation in the United States Virgin Islands">Transportation in the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Henry_E._Rohlsen_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry E. Rohlsen International Airport">Henry E. Rohlsen International Airport</a> serves St. Croix and the <a href="/wiki/Cyril_E._King_Airport" title="Cyril E. King Airport">Cyril E. King International Airport</a> serves St. Thomas and St. John.
</p><p>The U.S. Virgin Islands is the only US jurisdiction that drives on the left. This was inherited from what was then-current practice on the islands at the time of the 1917 transfer of the territory to the United States from Denmark. However, because most cars in the territory are imported from the mainland United States, the cars in the territory are <a href="/wiki/Left-hand_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Left-hand drive">left-hand drive</a>.
</p><p>As in other US territories, U.S. Virgin Islands mail service is handled by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a>, using the two-character state code "VI" for domestic mail delivery.<sup id="cite_ref-WebMastersVI-TouristTips_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WebMastersVI-TouristTips-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USPS-abbrs_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USPS-abbrs-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USPS-VI-info_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USPS-VI-info-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/ZIP_code" class="mw-redirect" title="ZIP code">ZIP codes</a> are in the 008xx range.<sup id="cite_ref-USPS-VI-info_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USPS-VI-info-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
As of  January&#160;2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, specifically assigned codes include 00801–00805 (St Thomas),<sup id="cite_ref-Zip-00801_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zip-00801-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
00820–00824 (Christiansted),<sup id="cite_ref-Zip-00820_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zip-00820-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
00830–00831 (St. John),<sup id="cite_ref-Zip-00830_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zip-00830-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
00840–00841 (Frederiksted),<sup id="cite_ref-Zip-00840_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zip-00840-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
and 00850–00851 (Kingshill).<sup id="cite_ref-Zip-00850_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zip-00850-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
The islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">North American Numbering Plan</a>, using <a href="/wiki/Area_code_340" title="Area code 340">area code 340</a>, and island residents and visitors are able to call most <a href="/wiki/Toll-free_telephone_number" title="Toll-free telephone number">toll-free US numbers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WebMastersVI-TouristTips_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WebMastersVI-TouristTips-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. Virgin Islands are located in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Standard_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Standard Time">Atlantic Standard Time</a> zone and do not participate in <a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">daylight saving time</a>. When the mainland United States is on Standard Time, the U.S. Virgin Islands are one hour ahead of Eastern Standard Time. When the mainland United States is on daylight saving time, Eastern Daylight Time is the same as Atlantic Standard Time.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Demographics of the United States Virgin Islands">Demographics of the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StJohnTrunkBay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/StJohnTrunkBay.jpg/220px-StJohnTrunkBay.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/StJohnTrunkBay.jpg/330px-StJohnTrunkBay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/StJohnTrunkBay.jpg/440px-StJohnTrunkBay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StJohnTrunkBay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Trunk_Bay" title="Trunk Bay">Trunk Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">St. John</a></div></div></div>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical population</th></tr><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">±%</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1970 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">62,468</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">—&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1980 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">96,569</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+54.6%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1990 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">101,809</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+5.4%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">108,612</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+6.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2010 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">106,405</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−2.0%</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In 2010 the U.S. Virgin Islands had a population of 106,405.<sup id="cite_ref-GR2_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> There are 40,648 households, and 26,636 families.
</p><p>In 2010 there were 40,648 households out of which 34.7% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 33.2% were married couples living together, 24.9% had a female householder with no husband present, and 34.5% were non-families. 30.2% of all households were made up of individuals and 6.3% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.64 and the average family size was 3.34.
</p><p>In the territory, the population in 2010 was distributed with 31.6% under the age of 18, 8.0% from 18 to 24, 27.1% from 25 to 44, 24.9% from 45 to 64, and 8.4% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 33 years. For every 100 females, there were 91.4 males. For every 100 females ages 18 and up, there were 87.7 males. The annual population growth is −0.12%.
</p><p>The literacy rate for the adult population was 94.9% in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The racial makeup of the U.S. Virgin Islands was:<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Black or <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a>: 76.0%  (66.1% Non-Hispanic Black)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a>: 15.7% (13.5% <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">Non-Hispanic Whites</a>)</li>
<li>Asian: 1.4%</li>
<li>Mixed: 2.1%</li>
<li>Other: 4.5%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Hispanic or Latino</a> of any race: 17.4%  (10.3% <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Rican</a>, 5.4% <a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="People of the Dominican Republic">Dominican</a>)</li></ul>
<p>Many residents can trace their ancestry to other Caribbean islands, especially Puerto Rico and the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>. The territory is largely Afro-Caribbean in origin.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>English is currently the dominant language and Spanish is spoken by about 17% of the population. Other languages are spoken by 11% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
English has been the predominant language since 1917 when the islands were transferred from Denmark to the United States. Under Danish rule, the official language was Danish, but it was solely the language of administration and spoken by Danes, a tiny minority of the overall population that primarily occupied administrative roles in colonial Danish West Indian society. However, place names and surnames of Denmark-Norway origin still remain among natives.
</p><p>Although the U.S. Virgin Islands was a Danish possession during most of its colonial history, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a> never was a spoken language among the populace, black or white, as the majority of plantation and slave owners were of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Even during Danish ownership, Dutch was more common, at least during some of those 245 years, specifically on St. Thomas and St. John. In St. Croix, English was the dominant language. St. Croix was owned by the French until 1733 when the island was sold to the Danish West Indian and Guinea Company. By 1741 there were five times as many English on the island as Danes. English Creole emerged on St. Croix more so than Dutch Creole, which was more popular on St. Thomas and St. John. Other languages spoken in the Danish West Indies included Irish, Scots, Spanish, and French, as well as Virgin Islands English Creole.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Creole" title="Virgin Islands Creole">Virgin Islands Creole English</a>, an English-based creole locally known as "dialect", is spoken in informal situations. The form of Virgin Islands Creole spoken on St. Croix, known as <i>Crucian</i>, is slightly different from that spoken on St. Thomas and St. John. Because the U.S. Virgin Islands are home to thousands of immigrants from across the Caribbean, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and various <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French creole</a> languages are also widely spoken.
</p><p>As of the 2000 census, 25.3% of persons over the age of five speak a language other than English at home. Spanish is spoken by 16.8% of the population and French is spoken by 6.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Orange"></div><div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 833.67445855047px; border-left-color:grey"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:grey"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:grey"></div><div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 272.37868371333px; border-left-color:DarkBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DarkBlue"></div><div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 199.34765443402px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div><div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:82.708057427456px 56.208337785213px 0 0; border-top-color:Blue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Blue"></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in the United States Virgin Islands (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Protestant (65.5%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Roman Catholic (27.1%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian (1.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Unaffiliated (3.7%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religion (1.9%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the dominant religion in the U.S. Virgin Islands. According to Pew Research Center, 94.8% of the population was Christian in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Episcopalian" class="mw-redirect" title="Episcopalian">Episcopalian</a> were the largest Christian denominations in the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Owing to both their Danish past and American present, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> on the islands has long been widespread. It was first introduced when <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> was brought to the islands in the Danish colonization. The Danish crown also allowed other religious traditions on the islands including <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravian Church</a> and other Protestant groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Scott_Latourette_1961_pp_278-79_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Scott_Latourette_1961_pp_278-79-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Historically, St. Thomas and St. Croix are known for missionary efforts undertaken by the <a href="/wiki/Moravian_missionaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Moravian missionaries">Moravian missionaries</a>. They were allowed on the islands by the Danish royal court, but came under scrutiny when they denounced <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Scott_Latourette_1961_pp_278-79_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Scott_Latourette_1961_pp_278-79-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-S&amp;H_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S&amp;H-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (March 2018)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A number of neo-Protestant traditions including <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostalism</a>, various <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Protestants">evangelical Protestants</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a> arrived later with the switch of allegiance from Denmark to the United States.
</p><p>There is also a strong <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> presence. <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">Rastafari</a> is also prevalent. St. Thomas is home to one of the oldest Jewish communities in the Western Hemisphere as <a href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> began to settle the island in the 18th century as traders and merchants. The <a href="/wiki/St._Thomas_Synagogue" title="St. Thomas Synagogue">St. Thomas Synagogue</a> in Charlotte Amalie is the second oldest synagogue on American soil and oldest in terms of continuous usage.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, the national average life expectancy was 79.61 years. It was 76.57 years for men and 82.83 for women.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Department_of_Education" title="Virgin Islands Department of Education">United States Virgin Islands Department of Education</a> serves as the territory's education agency, and has two school districts: <a href="/wiki/St._Thomas-St._John_School_District" title="St. Thomas-St. John School District">St. Thomas-St. John School District</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Croix_School_District" title="St. Croix School District">St. Croix School District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="University of the Virgin Islands">University of the Virgin Islands</a> provides higher education leading to associate's, bachelor's, and master's degrees, with campuses on St. Thomas and St. Croix.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Culture of the Virgin Islands">Culture of the Virgin Islands</a></div>
<p>The culture of the Virgin Islands reflects the various people that have inhabited the present-day U.S. Virgin Islands and <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, both despite their political separation having kept close cultural ties. The culture derives chiefly from <a href="/wiki/West_African" class="mw-redirect" title="West African">West African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> cultures, in addition to the influences from the immigrants from the Arab world, India and other Caribbean islands. The island was strongly influenced by the Dutch,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> French and Danish during the periods of control the island were under these powers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Music of the Virgin Islands">Music of the Virgin Islands</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The islands have a number of AM and FM radio stations (mostly on St. Thomas and St. Croix) broadcasting music, religious, and news programming.  (See <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_US_Territories" class="mw-redirect" title="List of radio stations in US Territories">List of radio stations in US Territories</a>.)  Full and low-power television stations are split between St. Thomas and St. Croix.  (See <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_stations_in_the_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="List of television stations in the U.S. Virgin Islands">List of television stations in the U.S. Virgin Islands</a>.)  Newspapers include:
</p>
<ul><li><i>The Avis</i>, printed daily on St. Croix.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Virgin_Islands_Daily_News" title="The Virgin Islands Daily News">The Virgin Islands Daily News</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> printed daily on St. Thomas.</li>
<li><i>St. John Tradewinds</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> distributed weekly on St. John.</li>
<li><i>St. Thomas – St. John This Week</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> online only.</li>
<li><i>St. Thomas Source</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> online only.</li>
<li><i>St. Croix Source</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> online only.</li>
<li><i>St. John On Island Times</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> news and information on St. John, USVI.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Public holidays in the United States Virgin Islands">Public holidays in the United States Virgin Islands</a></div>
<ul><li>January 1: New Year's Day</li>
<li>January 6: Three Kings Day</li>
<li>January (third Monday): Martin Luther King, Jr. Day</li>
<li>February (third Monday): Presidents' Day</li>
<li>March 31: <a href="/wiki/Transfer_Day" title="Transfer Day">Transfer Day</a> (celebrates the transfer of the islands from Denmark to the US)</li>
<li>April: Holy Thursday, Good Friday, Easter Monday</li>
<li>May: Memorial Day</li>
<li>July 3: <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Day#United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Emancipation Day">Emancipation Day</a></li>
<li>July 4: US Independence Day</li>
<li>September (first Monday): Labor Day</li>
<li>October (second Monday): Virgin Islands Puerto Rico Friendship Day/Columbus Day</li>
<li>November 1: <a href="/wiki/D._Hamilton_Jackson" title="D. Hamilton Jackson">D. Hamilton Jackson</a> Day (also known as "Liberty Day", or "Bull and Bread Day")</li>
<li>November 11: Veterans Day</li>
<li>November (fourth Thursday): Thanksgiving Day</li>
<li>December 25: Christmas</li>
<li>December 26: Christmas Second Day (also known as "Boxing Day")</li></ul>
<p>Virgin Islands government employees are also given administrative leave for St. Croix <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Carnival" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Carnival">carnival</a> events in January and St. Thomas carnival events in April/May.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
<cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.vinow.com/general_usvi/history/">"Virgin Islands History"</a>. <i>VI Now</i>. VInow.com. 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">February 15,</span> 2017</span>. <q>In the Danish West Indies slaves labored mainly on sugar plantations. Cotton, indigo and other crops were also grown. Sugar mills and plantations dotted the islands hilly landscapes. Each islands economy prospered through sugar plantations and slave trading. While St. John and St. Croix maintained a plantation economy, St. Thomas developed into a prosperous center of trade. Slave rebellion on St. John and St. Croix are well documented. Legitimate trade and business on St. Thomas influenced a different society where many more slaves were given freedom and an opportunity outside of plantation life.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=VI+Now&amp;rft.atitle=Virgin+Islands+History&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.vinow.com%2Fgeneral_usvi%2Fhistory%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUnited+States+Virgin+Islands" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
